                  </form>, said of spunger (<foreign lang="ar">وَارِش</foreign>), <hi rend="ital">He watched for the time of eating, in order that he might enter.</hi> (S.) And <foreign lang="ar">تحيّن الطَّعَامَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He watched for the time of the food</hi>]. (K voce <foreign lang="ar">حَضِرٌ</foreign>.) And <foreign lang="ar">تَحَيَّنْتُ رُؤْيَةَ فُلَانٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I watched for the time of seeing such a one.</hi> (TA.) And <foreign lang="ar">تحيّن وَقْتَ الصَّلَاةِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He sought</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to know</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the time of prayer.</hi> (TA.) [And accord. to Freytag's Lex.,

(TA.)    </entryFree>2a:T1dc4,<entryFree id="n9801" key="حِينٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">حِينٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">حين</orth>
                  </form> 
                  <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">دَهْرٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Time;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a time;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a space,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">period, of time;</hi> &amp;c.]: (K:) or, accord. to EshSháfi'ee, <hi rend="ital">time, from the beginning of the world to its end;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">دَهْرٌ</foreign>: (Az voce <foreign lang="ar">دَهْرٌ</foreign>:) or <hi rend="ital">a time,</hi> (Az, S, Mgh, Msb, K,) <hi rend="ital">in a vague sense,</hi> (Mgh, K,) applicable to <hi rend="ital">any time,</hi> (Az, K,) <hi rend="ital">little or much,</hi> (Mgh, Msb,) <hi rend="ital">long or short, that may be a year</hi> and <hi rend="ital">more:</hi> or [in some cases] particularly meaning <hi rend="ital">forty years:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">seven years:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">two years:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">six months:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">two months:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">any morning and evening:</hi> (K:) also <hi rend="ital">a space of time;</hi> (S, K;) as in the Kur lxxvi. I, (S,) and in the Kur xxxvii. 178: (K:) and <hi rend="ital">a continuous time:</hi> (Ham p. 381:) and the <hi rend="ital">day of resurrection;</hi> (K;) or the <hi rend="ital">coming to pass of the resurrection;</hi> as in the Kur xxxviii. last verse: (Mgh, TA:) or it has two meanings; namely, <hi rend="ital">a time of unknown limit,</hi> and also, as in the Kur xiv. 30, <hi rend="ital">six months:</hi> (Fr, Msb:) accord. to Er-Rághib, the <hi rend="ital">time of</hi> a thing's <hi rend="ital">arriving,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">coming,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">happening;</hi> having a vague meaning, and rendered particular, or special, by that to which it is prefixed: some say that it occurs applied in different ways: to <hi rend="ital">an appointed term;</hi> as that to which God makes one to live: and <hi rend="ital">a year;</hi> as in the Kur xiv. 30: and to the <hi rend="ital">time</hi> when an event takes place; as in the Kur xxx. 16: and to <hi rend="ital">time absolutely:</hi> accord. to El-Munáwee, in the [genuine] language of the Arabs, it is applied to [the <hi rend="ital">time of</hi>] <hi rend="ital">a glance of the eye,</hi> and <hi rend="ital">more than that,</hi> to <hi rend="ital">time without end:</hi> (TA:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَحْيَانٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) and pl. pl. <foreign lang="ar">أَحَايِينُ</foreign>; (S, * K;) as in the saying, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ يَفْعَلُ كَذَا أَحْيَانًا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">فِى الأَحَايِينِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Such a one does so at times,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">sometimes</hi>]. (S.) In the Kur [xiv. 30], <foreign lang="ar">تُؤْتِى</foreign>, <foreign lang="ar">أُكُلَهَا كُلَّ حِينٍ</foreign> means [<hi rend="ital">Which yieldeth its fruit</hi>] <hi rend="ital">every six months:</hi> (Fr, Msb, TA:) or <hi rend="ital">every year:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">every morning and evening:</hi> or, accord. to Az, <hi rend="ital">in every season, uninterruptedly.</hi> (TA.) <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n9801-1" target="مِحْيَانُ" n="1" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>شَىْءٍ</foreign>, also, means <foreign lang="ar">حِينُهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The time,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">season, of a thing</hi>]. (K.) [You say, <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى حِينٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">For a time,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">season.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">حِينًا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">At one time; sometime; at some time; awhile.</hi> (Mgh.) <foreign lang="ar">حِينَ</foreign> in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">قُمْتُ حِينَ قُمْتَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I stood in the time when thou stoodest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">I stood when thou stoodest,</hi>] is an adv. n. of time; (Msb;) [see also an ex. in a verse cited voce <foreign lang="ar">خَشَفَ</foreign>, and the remarks there subjoined:] and one may well employ in its place <foreign lang="ar">لَمَّا</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">إِذَا</foreign> (Msb, TA) and <foreign lang="ar">إِذْ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَتَى</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">سَاعَةَ</foreign> (TA) and <foreign lang="ar">وَقْتَ</foreign> (Msb, TA) and the like; but not, as many have said, <foreign lang="ar">حَيْثُ</foreign>; for this is an adv. n. of place. (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  When they make the two times to be distant, the one from the other, [i. e. the time of speaking and the time spoken of,] they do so by means of <foreign lang="ar">إذ</foreign>, and thus, (K,) they say <foreign lang="ar">حِينَئِذٍ</foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">At that time; then</hi>]: (S, K:) and sometimes they suppress the <foreign lang="ar">ء</foreign>, substituting for it <foreign lang="ar">ى</foreign>. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Sometimes, also, they prefix <foreign lang="ar">تَ</foreign> to <foreign lang="ar">حِينَ</foreign>; (S, TA;) and say <foreign lang="ar">لَا تَحِينَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">It is not,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">was not, a time</hi> [of such a thing; but this is generally written <foreign lang="ar">لَاتَ حِينَ</foreign>]; as in the Kur xxxviii. 2 [respecting which see art. <foreign lang="ar">ليت</foreign>]. (TA.) Aboo-Wejzeh Es-Saadee says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">اَلْعَاطِفُونَ تَحِينَ مَا مِنْ عَاطِفٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَالمُطْعِمُونَ زَمَانَ أَيْنَ المُطْعِوُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">The persons who return to the attack when there is none</hi> other <hi rend="ital">that returns to the attack,</hi> (as is said in the S and L in art. <foreign lang="ar">عطف</foreign>,) or it may mean <hi rend="ital">who act affectionately in the time when there is none</hi> other <hi rend="ital">that acts affectionately;</hi> as is said in the L in that art.;) <hi rend="ital">and the feeders in the time when</hi> it is said, <hi rend="ital">Where is the feeder?</hi>]: (S:) ISd says that <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> is thus prefixed to <foreign lang="ar">حين</foreign> like as it is in <foreign lang="ar">تَلَانَ</foreign> meaning <foreign lang="ar">الآنَ</foreign>: but IB says that Ibn-Es-Seeráfee cites the former hemistich thus: <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">اَلْعَاطِفُونَهْ حِينَ مَامِنْ عَاطِفٍ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [with the <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> of pausation]: and some say that the <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> of pausation is likened to the fem. <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, and is then made movent with fet-h. (TA. [See more in art. <foreign lang="ar">ليت</foreign>.])          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">حِينَةٌ</foreign>, in two places.    </entryFree>2b:T809,<entryFree id="n9804" key="حِينَةٌ" type="main">

      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n9804-1" target="حِينٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n9801"/></foreign>: you say, <foreign lang="ar">مَتَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">حِينَةُ نَاقَتِكَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">When is the time of the milking of thy she-camel?</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">كَمْ حِينَتُهَا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">How many times is she milked</hi>?
